<div id="review_1015363343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015363343" />
    <a title="Licha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614272-licha"><img alt="Licha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337135662p2/5614272.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1015363343?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Licha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Licha" href="/user/show/5614272-licha">Licha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780453005074" href="/book/show/11606.The_Bachman_Books">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614272-licha?shelf=favorite-author">favorite-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1015363343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12206362273699602547">The Long Walk finalizes the first four Bachman books for me. For sake of brevity, I reviewed the other three stories individually.<br/><br/>I’m a little torn by what to rate this particular story. The first half started out very strong. I’d give it 3.5 stars. What an insane story! One hundred boys are on a walk of endurance for their lives, and only one can survive. This is not just a simple 10 mile marathon. No. This walk crosses at least three states. The boys are not allowed to go under four miles, ste</span>
  <span id="freeText12206362273699602547" style="display:none">The Long Walk finalizes the first four Bachman books for me. For sake of brevity, I reviewed the other three stories individually.<br /><br />I’m a little torn by what to rate this particular story. The first half started out very strong. I’d give it 3.5 stars. What an insane story! One hundred boys are on a walk of endurance for their lives, and only one can survive. This is not just a simple 10 mile marathon. No. This walk crosses at least three states. The boys are not allowed to go under four miles, step out of boundaries, ask for provisions other than canteens of water and one daily allowance of pureed paste-like food. Tuna in a tube. Delicious. They are not allowed to physically interfere with any of the boy’s walking progress. There are no bathroom breaks (yes, if you’ve got to go #2 or #3, you better do it quick and you will do it right there on the open road), no sleeping breaks, no rest breaks, and no first aid breaks. Three strikes within an hour, the boy will get killed. Every hour they walk without a strike can earn them back a strike. The goal is The Prize, anything you want at your beck and call. It’s the elusive goal that 99 boys will pay their lives with. So what went wrong for me?<br /><br />The story dragged after the second half. The story could have been a lot shorter and not missed a thing. It became very repetitive after a while. If King’s intention was to make me feel like I was literally walking that long walk with the boys, he succeeded. There were also many unanswered questions that I felt needed an explanation. I was able to overlook it in The Running Man, but in this story, I felt like there was some explaining to do.<br /><br />--The rules of the game are never fully explained. We learn a rule here and there but that’s about it. How did this sadist contest come to be created? What world were the boys living in that boys would willingly sign up to participate? What world are people living in that they are accepting spectators, cheering the boys on and even betting on which boy will make it to the end? Who exactly is the Mayor?<br /><br />--Can someone really walk that long, without any breaks of any sort? I would have been shot after the first few miles if not a couple. It started getting harder to believe the longer they walked, especially in the conditions given.<br /><br />--Too much unbelievable conversation between the boys goes on. It didn’t ring true to teenage boys. They sounded like old men who have lived through quite a bit. Some of the conversation seemed mundane considering what was at stake. The conversations also didn’t reveal anything about the boys that endeared me to any of them. There wasn’t any one in particular I could root for.<br /><br />The end was a little anticlimactic for me. By that point I was wishing all the boys would just fall from sheer exhaustion. The second half of this was 1.5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12206362273699602547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5432532740830129510">What a mixed bag. I loved The Long Walk with its imaginative plot and great character study. Who would have thought that a book about walking can be so intense and gruesome? Hunger Games has nothing on this bad boy. Roadwork, on the other hand, kind of bored me. I could see what it was trying to do - mainly a slow unraveling of the main character into madness, - but I just couldn't focus on the story. What is the motivation? Why the stubbornness? I understand that the house represented more than</span>
  <span id="freeText5432532740830129510" style="display:none">What a mixed bag. I loved The Long Walk with its imaginative plot and great character study. Who would have thought that a book about walking can be so intense and gruesome? Hunger Games has nothing on this bad boy. Roadwork, on the other hand, kind of bored me. I could see what it was trying to do - mainly a slow unraveling of the main character into madness, - but I just couldn't focus on the story. What is the motivation? Why the stubbornness? I understand that the house represented more than just a material possession to this guy, but I could not sympathize with him or get behind his point of view. Running Man sort of returned to the glorious exploration of survival that I liked in the Long Walk, but again failed to completely engage me. The characters weren't as fleshed out, and the ending was sort of meh. <br /><br />To those unfamiliar with Richard Bachman's writing I can say that in my opinion Stephen King created this pseudonym as a no-pressure foray into psychological thrillers, rather than his usual horror genre. I'm kind of on the fence about these attempts, but will certainly recommend The Long Walk to anyone interested checking out that side of King. </span>

<div id="review_2118717072" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour"><img alt="J.M. Hushour" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442964894p2/17463213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2118717072?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.M. Hushour" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour">J.M. Hushour</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer652953851076622207">Three-stars is what the whole volume averages out to. I'll rate the four novels individually:<br/><br/>Rage: 1 star. It's puerile and terrible. Textbook teen angst and resultant school shooting. A yawner considering the quality of the next one...<br/><br/>The Long Walk: 4-5 stars? Hard to say. It is inventive, nerve-wracking and weird. Whereas the dialogue sometimes fumbles (what teenager calls anyone 'whoreson'? wonders the main character himself) and some of the characters are wafer thin, it's very original and r</span>
  <span id="freeText652953851076622207" style="display:none">Three-stars is what the whole volume averages out to. I'll rate the four novels individually:<br /><br />Rage: 1 star. It's puerile and terrible. Textbook teen angst and resultant school shooting. A yawner considering the quality of the next one...<br /><br />The Long Walk: 4-5 stars? Hard to say. It is inventive, nerve-wracking and weird. Whereas the dialogue sometimes fumbles (what teenager calls anyone 'whoreson'? wonders the main character himself) and some of the characters are wafer thin, it's very original and rip-offable. The plot is deceptively simple: walk until you win or die. Then you basically get whatever you want.<br /><br />Roadwork: 1 star. The only one I couldn't finish. Essentially the film "Falling Down" with a lower body count and little of the wit.<br /><br />The Running Man: 4-5 stars. Light-years from the film adaptation and eminently superior. I'm not sure about this, but this novel seems to serve as a rip-off point for many inferior dystopian products. "The Hunger Games", which is awful, basically ripped this off: in a poverty-stricken future controlled by rich, fascists, people starve and starve for entertainment. 'The Running Man' is a game show where you run from Hunters and try to survive, televised live. This is also darkly hilarious, with a protagonist who is shitty. There is little pretty, here. I loved it!<br /><br />2/4 isn't bad. You can sort of see the hints of King's transition writing these over a multi-year span. Definitely worth reading for the two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="652953851076622207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2409817581" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2409817581" />
    <a title="Russ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71984867-russ"><img alt="Russ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596247106p2/71984867.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2409817581?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Russ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Russ" href="/user/show/71984867-russ">Russ</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451147363" href="/book/show/228162.The_Bachman_Books">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2409817581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer471794579981949435">If this was a short story book I would have given it an overall rating but since its four novellas I figured it was best to rate each story. <br/><br/>Rage- 3 stars- I don't really know what to say about this one. I almost don't remember it because it was so short and didn't really have anything that stood out as significant. I don't remember hating it either so ya that's Rage. <br/><br/>The Long Walk- 2 stars- I was really expecting this one to be my favorite of the four because of all the good stuff I heard about</span>
  <span id="freeText471794579981949435" style="display:none">If this was a short story book I would have given it an overall rating but since its four novellas I figured it was best to rate each story. <br /><br />Rage- 3 stars- I don't really know what to say about this one. I almost don't remember it because it was so short and didn't really have anything that stood out as significant. I don't remember hating it either so ya that's Rage. <br /><br />The Long Walk- 2 stars- I was really expecting this one to be my favorite of the four because of all the good stuff I heard about it. If not my favorite I was at least expecting to enjoy it. I hate to say that I had a lot of trouble even getting through it. It reminded me a lot of "The Road" which I also did not like. It had that same dull atmosphere the whole time with a lot of repetitiveness. It was really hard for me yo even care about any of the characters. So in the end it was just that...a LONG walk. <br /><br />Roadwork- 5 stars- Now this one I was expecting to be my least favorite and go figure not only was it my favorite of the four but one of my all time favorites. Not only that but George is one of my all time favorite characters. There are parts when you feel so sorry for him and want him to turn his life around. Then there are parts when you are falling down the rabbit hole with him and rooting for him to go down in a blaze of glory. I also really loved the interactions he had with other characters. All in all the was a gem I was not expecting. <br /><br />The Running Man- 3 stars- This was definitely better than the movie but still just OK for me. This is one of them books where if it was a couple hundred pages longer it probably would have been great. It felt a little rushed to me. You come across characters that could have been more fleshed out were the book longer. The best part of this book was the last like 50 pages with a great ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="471794579981949435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7038223805376606380">Rage - The banned Bachman book that is more notorious for being banned than - the student loses it at school, kills and takes a class hostage story. Still a story very much ahead of its time when it was written. 4 out of 12<br/><br/>The Long Walk - This book haunts me, an exceptionally horrifying read. 100 teenage boys compete in the Long Walk endurance race… where there can only be one winner and the losers die or are killed! So far ahead of it's time, as King/Bachman takes the reality TV show to its log</span>
  <span id="freeText7038223805376606380" style="display:none">Rage - The banned Bachman book that is more notorious for being banned than - the student loses it at school, kills and takes a class hostage story. Still a story very much ahead of its time when it was written. 4 out of 12<br><br>The Long Walk - This book haunts me, an exceptionally horrifying read. 100 teenage boys compete in the Long Walk endurance race… where there can only be one winner and the losers die or are killed! So far ahead of it's time, as King/Bachman takes the reality TV show to its logical conclusion? 10 out of 12.<br><br>The Running Man - Completely different to the film… Ben Richards is compelled to take part in The Running Man in this dystopia, to save the lives of his family… but the Games have no idea just how difficult Richards will be to kill. Dark, thrilling and definitely hardcore dystopian horror classic! Also King's blazing attack on consumerism and capitalism inability to truly help the masses? 8 out of 12.<br><br>King/Bachman's tale of a white suburban male finally having one First World problem too many and going out with a bang! Like Rage a pretty poor book, albeit written by a very young and busy King. 3 out of 12<br><br>Two stinkers and 2 pots of gold, still only gives an average of about 6 out of 12.<br>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1577804661ra/28694173.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_383137'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/383137.Misery"><img alt="Misery" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1174341325l/383137.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sotrYIGm/iL7swTzpYCGK/Awg+cKb+uBdfO1WLm6KhCkJb8Frlo/+VCV69bT1zevKLvhz4Qzsfe4gLHVBLvMDw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5858.Richard_Bachman">About Richard Bachman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5858.Richard_Bachman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1289702449p3/5858.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5858.Richard_Bachman">Richard Bachman
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,284
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13476423485386194928">This is a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King' title='Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stephen King</a> pseudonym.<br/><br/>At the beginning of Stephen King's career, the general view among publishers was that an author was limited to one book per year, since publishing more would be unacceptable to the public. King therefore wanted to write under another name, in order to increase his publication without over-saturating the market for the King "brand". He convinced his publisher, Signe</span>
  <span id="freeText13476423485386194928" style="display:none">This is a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a> pseudonym.<br /><br />At the beginning of Stephen King's career, the general view among publishers was that an author was limited to one book per year, since publishing more would be unacceptable to the public. King therefore wanted to write under another name, in order to increase his publication without over-saturating the market for the King "brand". He convinced his publisher, Signet Books, to print these novels under a pseudonym.<br /><br />In his introduction to <i>The Bachman Books</i>, King states that adopting the nom de plume Bachman was also an attempt to make sense out of his career and try to answer the question of whether his success was due to talent or luck. He says he deliberately released the Bachman novels with as little marketing presence as possible and did his best to "load the dice against" Bachman. King concludes that he has yet to find an answer to the "talent versus luck" question, as he felt he was outed as Bachman too early to know. The Bachman book <i>Thinner</i> (1984) sold 28,000 copies during its initial run—and then ten times as many when it was revealed that Bachman was, in fact, King.<br /><br />The pseudonym King originally selected (Gus Pillsbury) is King's maternal grandfather's name, but at the last moment King changed it to Richard Bachman. Richard is a tribute to crime author Donald E. Westlake's long-running pseudonym Richard Stark. (The surname Stark was later used in King's novel <i>The Dark Half</i>, in which an author's malevolent pseudonym, "George Stark", comes to life.) Bachman was inspired by Bachman–Turner Overdrive, a rock and roll band King was listening to at the time his publisher asked him to choose a pseudonym on the spot.<br /><br />King provided biographical details for Bachman, initially in the "about the author" blurbs in the early novels. Known "facts" about Bachman were that he was born in New York, served a four-year stint in the Coast Guard, which he then followed with ten years in the merchant marine. Bachman finally settled down in rural central New Hampshire, where he ran a medium-sized dairy farm, writing at night. His fifth novel was dedicated to his wife, Claudia Inez Bachman, who also received credit for the bogus author photo on the book jacket. Other "facts" about the author were revealed in publicity dispatches from Bachman's publishers: the Bachmans had one child, a boy, who died in an unfortunate, Stephen King-ish type accident at the age of six, when he fell through a well and drowned. In 1982, a brain tumour was discovered near the base of Bachman's brain; tricky surgery removed it. After Bachman's true identity was revealed, later publicity dispatches (and about the author blurbs) revealed that Bachman died suddenly in late 1985 of "cancer of the pseudonym, a rare form of schizonomia".<br /><br />King dedicated Bachman's early books—<i>Rage (1977), The Long Walk (1979), Roadwork (1981)</i>, and <i>The Running Man</i> (1982)—to people close to him. The link between King and his shadow writer was exposed after a Washington, D.C. bookstore clerk, Steve Brown, noted similarities between the writing styles of King and Bachman. Brown located publisher's records at the Library of Congress which included a document naming King as the author of one of Bachman's novels. Brown wrote to King's publishers with a copy of the documents he had uncovered, and asked them what to do. Two weeks later, King telephoned Brown personally and suggested he write an article about how he discovered the truth, allowing himself to be interviewed. King has taken full ownership of the Bachman name on numerous occasions, as with the republication of the first four Bachman titles as <i> The Bachman Books: Four Early Novels by Stephen King</i> in 1985. The introduction, titled "Why I Was Bachman," details the whole Bachman/King story.<br /><br />Source: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Bachmanhttps://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Bachman">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13476423485386194928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
